---
title: "Added Gnome Shell, where did Unity go?"
date: 2015-01-29
forum: Desktop Environments
---

### Post by eipapp on 2015-01-29
Have a rather odd situation I hope someone can help me with. I re-installed Ubuntu 14.04 LTS on Tuesday (01/27) which I had previously running on my machine. 
Upon completion, I then added Gnome Shell 3.12.
However, today (01/29) when I attempted to log out of Gnome and log into Unity, the option to do so was not there on the dropdown menu. 
What in the world might have happened ? Why do I no longer have the option of swithching between the desktops ?
My only available option now appears to be Gnome and nothing else.
Any help in getting my Unity back would be greatly appreciated.

Thanks,
Bruce

---

### Post by kc1di on 2015-01-30
Hi eipapp,

I don't believe Gnome shell and unity are compatible on the same install.  If you install gnome shell it overwrites files that are needed by Unity. 
and vice versa.  

sorry.

You can try to re-install unity desktop with this command ```
sudo apt-get install ubuntu-desktop ubuntu-settings
```
But it will break gnome 3. Good luck

---

### Post by eipapp on 2015-01-30
Dave, I'm afraid I will have to disagre with you on this one even though you clearly have much more knowledge and experience than I do. The fact is I was running Unity and Gnome for months before this happened. I frequently switched between Unity and Gnome with absolutely no problem. I was running Unity 14.04LTS along with Gnome Shell 3.10. It was only when I tried to upgrade to Unity 14.10 that the wheels came off. I was never able to get 14.10 up and running from the git to. That decision to upgarde turned out to be a disaster. That's was prompted the re-install I just did of 14.04LTS and Gnome. The ONLY thing I did differently this time from my original Unity/Gnome install is that I elected to go with Gnome 3.12 instead of 3.10. Don't know if that had anything to do with my current issue or not. Just sayin.......
For a while I was switching between Unity/Gnome/Gnome Metacity/Gnome com-piz & Cinnamon. Had no issues switching from one desktop enviornment to another. It was cake. Wish I had been smart enough to let well enough alone. Guess I'm one of those people who have to learn the hard way. :(

---

### Post by mc4man on 2015-01-30
See what these say, just  simulations - 
```
sudo apt-get -s install ubuntu-session
```
```
sudo apt-get -s install ubuntu-desktop
```
You definitely can have ubuntu(unity) & gnome-shell (repo version 3.10) installed together. Possibly 3.12 conflicts & removes something(s) that a ubuntu session needs.

(- though here I don't mix sessions for main user, just have another user set up for gnome-sessions, more because of theme issues, ect.

### Post by deadflowr on 2015-01-30
Interesting article here
[http://www.webupd8.org/2014/05/how-to-install-gnome-312-in-ubuntu.html](http://www.webupd8.org/2014/05/how-to-install-gnome-312-in-ubuntu.html)

But this tidbit is what I think you are seeing
> You may be wondering why I wrote "install GNOME 3.12 in Ubuntu GNOME 14.04"... well, that's because if you add this PPA on an Ubuntu (with Unity) 14.04 system, some Unity packages will be removed and thus, Unity will stop working.


So the GNOME 3 Staging PPA should only be used by Ubuntu GNOME 14.04 (don't add the PPA if you're using Unity!) users who know how to fix their system in case something goes wrong!


It is possible to use this PPA to install GNOME 3.12 on systems with Unity, but Unity will stop working and the instructions are more complicated, especially if you want to revert the changes, so I won't add instructions for such cases here.




Hope that helps.
